The Giver

~~~~~~Chapter 0: Tutorial Start~~~~~~

I felt so groggy. Ugh, I fucking hate that feeling—I wrenched my eyes open, trying to force my brain to wake up. Fuck, my whole head felt like it was full of lead. I tried to roll onto my side to look around, but as soon as I moved my right hand erupted in white-hot pain that cut straight through the grogginess. I hissed, drawing it to my chest and curling up into a fetal position. The pain died down after a couple seconds, decreasing to a throb that spiked a little when my heart beat. I took a shaky breath, flexing my other hand and, finding it unbroken, propped myself up.

Sensory input began flooding my mind; the slight whiff of mildew in the olfactory flood of bleach, the distant echoes of screams and crying entering and leaving harmony with the just-audible buzz of the lights in the hallway, the chill that had already seeped into my bones as springs from the mattress dug into me. It was a little more overwhelming than normal, but what was worse was the memories of how I got here.

I felt my lip curl as I remembered—Jimmy. That fucker… he’d BEATEN me!

I started shaking with the desire to scream, or punch somebody; I had been thwarted by a walking muscle with a pair of Goddamn testicles for a brain! Months crafting my empire, carefully laying down every piece of the plan, fucking GONE in an INSTANT! I could still feel the air thrumming with electricity as the moron of the century glared at me in confused anger and shouted, asking why I’d done it and I’d been happy to explain exactly why as the sweet, sweet feeling of victory coursed through me at how fucking stupid everybody else was and of course he didn’t care about how fucking dumb he was how could he possibly understand and ha he was calling me a loser now that’s fucking rich how long has it been raining my clothes are soaked through I knew exactly the right words to really twist the knife before suddenly I was fighting him I just had to hurt him somehow but it wasn’t working that crunching in my hand probably wasn’t a good sign and then I was tumbling through space as terror overtook my mind before everything went dark.

A shriek split the buzzing drone of florecent lighting made me flinch—this time, it wasn’t distant. Then, “Fuckin’ shut it!” followed by a sharp smack! and a whimper. Footsteps receded into the depths of the building.

I sat very still for a while, trying to bottle up a new, inexplicable urge to cry. Jesus, like I’m fucking Femme Boy. I squeezed my eyes shut, hanging onto that thought—anything to distract. Petey crying when I punched him for beating me at his dumb video game, screaming when I shoved him off the top of the slide, sniffling pathetically after I’d kicked him in the balls this year. I rolled my eyes to myself—you’d think somebody as relatively not-dumb as the others would be able to avoid doing stupid shit, but hey, he’s always been crap at avoiding trouble.

As the hours ticked by, the pit of my stomach bubbled and frothed to the point that I started digging my fingers into the palm of my broken hand to keep myself from screaming or, even worse, crying. I didn’t want to upset the guard or undignifiy myself by adding to the insanity soundscape. After all, I had a revenge scheme to hatch.

Hopkins would fucking PAY.

I passed out on my cot on June 2nd, 2007. Maybe I couldn’t get out, but God as my fucking witness I would drag Jimmy down with me.

~~~

When I finally came back into consciousness, I wasn’t sure why I was grateful for the untethered feeling that came with waking up. Usually I hate that feeling—one of the many reasons I avoid sleeping as much as humanly possible.

But eventually, reality came rushing back in—I’d had the whole school under my thumb until the King of the Idiots had shown up and fucked it all up and.. fucking hell, I haven’t wanted to cry since.. I don’t even know. Christ, Petey must’ve infected me with something—soon I’ll be sobbing at the drop of a hat.

Well, enough lying around; time to start planning. Sure, my life might be ruined, but I wasn’t about to let that keep me from destroying Hopkins’ life, too. I sighed, bringing my hand up to rub at my eyes sleepily—this time I wasn’t even starting from square one. I’d need to suck up big-time if I wanted to get anywhere. I yawned and stretched my arms out. At least this cot wasn’t as uncomfortable as I would’ve expected–

I snapped my eyes open. My hand was broken yesterday . I pulled it back from my face, taking a closer look. The leather strap on my wrist was there like it always is, and I couldn’t feel any pain coming from that hand when I flexed it gingerly. Weird. Had somebody come in and injected it with pain killers or something? I wouldn’t put it past this place. Still, probably best to treat it carefully, just to be on the safe side.

I dropped my hand and closed my eyes, sighing, almost wishing I was full of those drugs from yesterday. Then I’d just want to lie here and not think; playing Hopkins for a day didn’t sound too bad at this rate. I shook my head and moved to get out of bed, intent on splashing my face with some water to wake up. No rest for the wicke—I did a double-take when I was finally able to take in my surroundings.

I wasn’t in a dingy, claustrophobic cell. I was in my dorm room.

I gaped at everything open-mouthed, like somehow that might change what I was seeing. Petey was even asleep on the other side of the room, like everything was totally normal! I sat rooted to the spot for some time, my mind spinning around in circles. At some point, his stupid alarm clock started talking quietly about the local traffic, and he rolled out of bed. His greeting of, “Oh, hey Gary—morning,” managed to cut through my swirling vortex of thoughts. I snapped my head to see him yawning and stretching.

He didn’t even glance at me as he padded over to his wardrobe. …seriously? No reaction at all? “..Not surprised to see me, Petey?” He couldn’t have forgotten what happened; it’s not like he was pumped to the gills with sedatives yesterday.

He cocked his head in confusion as he started pulling his PJs off. “Hm? What do you —” Here he was interrupted by a large yawn before continuing. “—mean?” I tried to not let my annoyance show.

Jesus Christ, even early in the morning he can’t be this stupid! I got up, moving over to my own wardrobe and affecting a conversational tone, keeping my panic under wraps. “ Well …” I began rifling through my clothes, taking care to use my left hand. “I would’ve thought you’d be surprised to see somebody who got shipped off to the House for Crazies yesterday,” I shrugged casually, but kept a careful eye on his expression.

Seemed like he was finally waking up, because he turned to face me directly—but he was more ‘confused’, not the ‘terrified’ I’d been expecting. “What? Do… uh.. you mean somebody got put in Happy Volts?” His face suddenly shifted to what could best be described as horrified. I smirked; there we go! “Wait, you mean a student!?”Hm. Guess not.

Seemed I would have spell it out for him—just like he needs fucking everything spelled out for him. “Wow, Petey, that’s pretty mean of you to say!” I clutched at my chest and did my best to ignore the cold dread that was still churning in my gut at the fact that I was going to spend the rest of my days locked up. “Am I really just ‘a student’ to you? And here I thought we were friends....” I then mock-pouted, fluttering my eyelashes, making sure to enjoy how uncomfortable he looked at the statement. Heh, that never gets old.

Even so, he recovered soon, oscillating between horror and confusion. “Wait, wait… are you saying you got put in there?” I rolled my eyes, automatically reaching out to grab something.

“Seriously Femme Boy, even you had to notice the showdown your boyfriend and I ha– shit ! ” I yanked my hand back as I bumped it against something in the wardrobe. But it hadn’t hurt. I frowned, flexing it a little less gingerly now. It felt fine—and now that I examined it more closely, it really didn’t look broken; wouldn’t it be discolored or swollen?

From across the room, Petey groaned at the ‘boyfriend’ comment. “Whatever man—what ‘showdown’? Is this about that new kid you’ve been talking about?” I snapped my gaze to him, but he was too busy tugging his pants on to notice my intense scrutiny.

“…what ‘new kid’?” I returned my attention to my right hand, using the left to press into it. There had to be something wrong with it—it had been so painful yesterday.

“You know, um.. Jamey? Timmy?” I turned my head toward him very slowly. How could he have forgotten Hopkins’ name ! ? He snapped his fingers a couple of times before saying “Oh, was it Jimmy?” and looking over at me expectantly as he buttoned up his stupid, girly shirt.

I was having an increasingly difficult time hiding my confusion. I only just managed to maintain a deadpan tone for my next line. “Yes. Jimmy. Jimmy Hopkins.”

I turned back to my wardrobe, grabbing my usual school uniform automatically as a buzzing noise began to fill my head. Using my right hand didn’t hurt at all —dressing helped me try and sort out my thoughts. One: my hand was broken yesterday, and today it wasn’t. Two: I went to bed in a fucking insanity asylum yesterday and today I woke up at school. Three: yesterday, Hopkins was the–here I paused to shudder–king of the school, and today not even Moron Lover Kowalski knows who he is. But what the hell did it all mean?

An innocent comment broke through my thoughts for the second time that morning. “Hey Gary, you okay? You’re not talking much…” I turned to Petey after pulling my sweater-vest on, the ritual of dressing finally complete. He added, a bit jokingly, “Not that I’m complaining.”

He fidgeted uncomfortably when my only reaction was to stare at him intently. Gathering information was probably the best course of action. “…what’s today’ s date? ”

He quirked an eyebrow suspiciously, but luckily he had enough brains to look at his watch. “It’s, uh… the ninth. Of September?” But he didn’t seem satisfied. “You sure you’re okay? You look kinda… worried..” I nodded distractedly, busy drowning in my own thoughts.

Holy shit

HOLY SHIT

Was I back at the beginning of the year somehow? I’ve always been a stickler for logic, and all the evidence pointed to fucking time travel?!?

A grin spread slowly across my face. I was free! I could do it again! Do it right this time!

As soon as I felt the beginnings of consciousness, I clawed my way out of sleep until I was fully awake. Failure. AGAIN. I punched my pillow in frustration, desperately wishing it was the moron’s face instead. I stopped, breathing heavily. The pillow was mocking me, I could fucking see it. “SHUT UP , MORON! ” Blindly hurling the fluffy object across the room, I got out of bed and strode over to my wardrobe and started pulling clothing on at random. I didn’t give a shit how I looked—I just wanted to shake Hopkins and get some ANSWERS. “How’s he fucking doing it!?” I asked myself as I wrestled with my pants.

“Uh.. doing what?” I started, noticing Femme Boy’s worried gaze for the first time. He was also clutching the pillow I’d thrown.

I frowned, then sighed. “Nothing, Petey,” No reason to make him suspicious so early on. I beamed at him reassuringly. “I’m just excited that the new kid is arriving today!”

He bought it, nodding in agreement as he smiled sleepily. “Oh, yeah, you wanna be friends with him, right?” He finally got out of bed, walking over to his own wardrobe and stifling a yawn. “I was thinking we could all be friends, you know? Sounds like nobody else” I tuned out the rest, instead staring down at the floor as I sat down, pants around my ankles for the moment. What was I doing wrong ? I ’d tried this twenty times and it hadn’t fucking worked once. I’d gotten Jimmy to side with me this last time, but at the last second he had turned the tables on me and started working against me. I’d even died six times! I shuddered as the sickening crunch from Hopkins’ body falling on my ribcage from this last try sounded through my head again. I hadn’t died immediately, but I’d struggled so much with the paramedic staff at the end that they’d kept dropping me. “…Hey, you alright? Need some help?” I snapped out of my revere to see Peter Kowalski with a worried expression kneeling in front of me, his hand outstretched. I accepted the hand entirely automatically—for some reason my brain took the time to note that the light in our room was framing Petey in a halo. Pulling me to my feet, he gave me an odd look before asking, “Are you sure you’re all right? You seem really out of it,” I finally snapped my gaze to his face, giving him my full attention.

What was I even doing? I had a plan to make. Twenty-first time’s the charm, right? “Yeah. Yeah I’ m fine, ” Snatching my hand back from his, I turned around to leave the room, before promptly face-planting onto the floor because my pants were still down around my ankles. “ Oof! ”

There was a pause before Petey started snickering. “Yeah, you’re tooootally fine!” I scrambled back up to my feet, yanking my undone pants back up. That little fuck.

Glaring at him out the corner of my eye, I sneered, “Like what you see, Femme Boy?” That cut off his laughing.

Instead, he grimaced, turning away to finish getting dressed, adding, “Ew! Come on man, don’t be gross,” I just laughed. Man, laughing felt so good!

As I finished buckling my belt and grabbing my keys, I called over my shoulder, “Try not to think about me too much out there, Femme Boy—it might show~!” I snickered at his whine through the paper-thin door.

Turning to go downstairs, I switched gears and again considered my dilemma. I needed to figure out what the fuck Jimmy was doing to constantly outwit me.... But how could I do that? Glaring as a Bully shoved past me, I realized that what I really lack is information. I just don’t know enough about Jimmy and how he responds to what I do—but it’s not like I can just follow the moron around day in and day out, that’d get boring real fast… right?

Then again, maybe there is a way to follow him around… Surveillance equipment, perhaps? Seeing Jimmy round the corner, I prepared to give the whole newcomer spiel. Wouldn’t hurt to give it a try—I’d only need to do it a few times, anyway. Then I’ll have all the information I need! I grinned as I commented that Jimmy was all pent up—he had better watch it this time; I was fucking on to him now!

~~~

The distant claps of thunder reminded me an awful lot of the tolling of bells. I automatically recited my lines—rather calmly, this time around. “The thing is, if I win, you’re just another punk....” I sucked in a deep breath, taking a moment to admire the view—I don’t usually come up here except for this—before shrugging as I continued, “but if you win, you’ll be sent away even faster for beating up the Head Boy,” Granted, by this point Petey had probably figured out how to get Crabblesnitch on his side, but still. I wanted to make sure this loop was as close to the first as possible.

And of course, the moron had his ‘confused’ face—the one that looks like he’s thinking whut wat duh? — on, and asked the pivotal question: “Why’d you do it, Gary!?”

I ’d been waiting ages for this! Clapping my hands in delight, I replied, “ OH, I ’m so happy you asked, Hopkins!” I rubbed my hands together excitedly. “ See, I ’ve been trying to figure this out for..” Pause for a few quick calculations. “..about fifteen years now. And I finally did it!”

Jimmy interrupted with an impatient growl. “Just get to the fucking point already!”

I held my hands up in a mock ‘surrender’ gesture. “All right, take a chill pill, why don’t you, Jimmy-boy?” I chuckled at my private joke as I paced back and forth on the construction scaffolding. “You see Jimmy, the fact is that you’re an idiot,” I held up a hand, stopping his objections. “Don’t try to deny it, it’s true. But here’s the more amazing thing—I still lost!” I stopped pacing, letting that sink into the King Idiot’s thick skull. His face gained even more ‘ wut ’.

“..you lost?” Jimmy blinked. Clearly, this had been the last thing he’d been expecting. “…so what, are you giving up?”

I shrugged, stifling the urge to start cackling madly. “In a way. It’s not like I’ll be around for the next few days anyway. Now, if I could continue?”

Jimmy glanced around the empty rooftop, as if checking to see if anybody else was seeing this shit. “Um, sure?”

I grinned, resuming my pacing. “You see, moron; the reason you were able to beat me so many times was, hilariously, as simple as you are! It was Petey!” Understanding was finally starting to bloom in the moron’s eyes.

“What? What the fuck are you talk– ” I held up a hand again, interrupting him.

“Now, now Jimmy! Credit where credit is due; Petey was the only reason you beat me, don’t deny it. Hell, the little trooper’s probably already gone to the police by now!” Jimmy shifted uncomfortably—I couldn’t blame him, if I’d had to rely on fucking Femme Boy Kowalski to do all my thinking for me, I’d probably just curl up and die. Not that that would do me much good nowadays, but still.

Jimmy frowned. “Yeah, Petey helped me… but so what? That doesn’t change anything!”

The dumbass had a point. “I suppose you’re right, it doesn’t change anything—not for you, at least,” I let my face split in a wide smile. “But it changes everything for me!” I shook my head, laughing at the sheer absurdity of it all. “I mean, can you fucking believe it!? Fucking Femme Boy !?! ” I actually slapped a hand across my knee, practically guffawing at this point. Christ, I couldn’t even remember the last time I’d laughed this hard!

And now, Jimmy was pissed again. “Whad’ya mean by that? What, is Pete not smart enough for your stupid fucking standards or something?”

I managed to reign it in so it was just giggling. “No, you see he IS smart! That’s why it’s so fucking brilliant!” I resumed my frantic pacing, gesticulating almost at random. “Petey’s literally the only person in this fucking town who actually has enough brains to mess with my plans, and he’s the only person I’d NEVER fucking suspect!” I stopped again, shaking my head before pressing both my palms into my forehead. “I just can’t get over it! I mean —” I lifted my head to try and explain how ridiculous this situation is. “I live in his fucking room and I NEVER considered he might betrey me! Not once!!”

I would’ve happily continued talking about this subject for quite a while, but Jimmy decided to interject at that point. “So… you giving up or what?” I stared at him for a few moments before sighing.

This had been the plan all along anyway. “I suppose so,” Suddenly, I had an idea and added, “Hey, can I talk to Petey before I get shipped off to Happy Volts? I’d love to know how he did all this!”

Jimmy blinked slowly. “ Happy Volts? ”

God are you kidding me? I groaned my most patronizing, “Obviously Happy Volts you moron! ” I started counting points off on my fingers as I rolled my eyes. “I got people expelled, unfairly, put several others into therapy, turned the school into a battleground and, oh! Let’s not mention all the property damage I caused,” I snorted, crossing my arms and raising one eyebrow at Jimmy, daring him to object. “I should hope I get put away after a stunt like that.”

He frowned, shuffling his feet. I smirked; heh, this really wasn’t going how he’d thought it would. “ Well, um .. okay, sure you can talk to him…” He suddenly glanced around at the scenery, as if only now noticing where we were.  “…why the fuck did you do all that ‘chasing you through the school’ shit if that’s all you wanted to say?”

I threw my hands up as I began making my way over the scaffolding back the way we’d come. “Because that’s what fucking happens, I don’t know. I tried to keep this one as close to the original as possible, so I figured I should follow tradition.”

Now Jimmy really was looking at me like I was bonkers. “…wow you are fucking insane. The fuck does any of that even mean?”

I just shot him a wink as I backed down a ladder, feeling the first droplets of rain on my skin. “Now Jimmy, don’t hurt yourself trying to understand it! Little Petey’s going to need you to make sure he doesn’t get beat up, after all,” My mind was occupied with more important matters now, anyway: Petey Femme Boy Kowalski. I had a brand-new puzzle to work through! I barely noticed the police officers circling the base of the tower like sharks as I made my way down. Now that I know his importance, it’ll be easy to get him to do my bidding—he’s got practically no spine anyway!

~~~~~~Chapter 1: Just Another Day for your Average Time Traveler~~~~~~

After two agonizing hours of sitting around with only the moron for company, Petey finally rounded the corner of the alleyway I’d parked on. Jimmy started trying to talk around his gag again, but he wasn’t fast enough—the zip ties had already made short work of Petey’s hands. He barely got in a, “Whoa, wh– ” before I’d thrown him in the backseat with Hopkins, hopped into the driver’s seat, and peeled away. One minute and counting.

Man, the waiting is my least favorite part of this step. I always feel like a cop will be the first person to round that corner. “Phew.. sheesh Femme Boy, you sure took your sweet time, didn’t you?” The speedometer was inching past sixty now—I wanted to be doing a hundred after we got out of serious accident possibility range, but for now I needed the precision to turn down streets without totaling the vehicle. The cops would be on me in forty-five seconds, so I needed as big a head start as I could muster.

There was a disorientated, “Wha–holy shit, what?” I could hear movement in the back before he stilled abruptly, noticing the gagged cries. “…Jimmy? What..” Then he stopped talking as he registered what I’d said. “..G-Gary?”

I grunted. The innocent confusion is cute, but I really needed to concentrate in the next fifteen seconds so we didn’t end up dead. “If you’ve got questions, save them for when distracting me won’t result in serious bodily trauma—okay, Pete?” I took a deep breath. He’d try and continue talking, but if my first evasive maneuver against these cops is a big one, he clams up big-time.

Police sirens started wailing, and I saw Petey’s head whip around at the sound. Seven seconds. “...What the hell?” He turned back around and pressed his face against the metal mesh that separated the backseat from the front seat. Two seconds. I tightened my grip in anticipation—this part is always fun. “What’s happ—”

I shouted, “Hold onto your butts, kiddos!” before turning the wheel sharply, causing the car to skid at an angle, just as two cop cars pulled up, sirens blaring. And would you look at that, my car was perfectly angled to speed through that gap; I floored it. “Woooo, hahaha!” Lucky for me, this car has pretty good horsepower. A few seconds of metal grinding against metal later, we made it through, sans the right-side rear-view mirror and a bit of paint. Still, all things considered that was one of my better attempts. I righted the steering wheel, and I could hear the contents of the backseat grunting and groaning as they hit the left side of the car as it straightened out and burned rubber out of town. I could take it easy for a few minutes now, thanks to some earlier tire sabotage. I flicked the siren on and headed off, shifting up to one-hundred. Mostly to myself I sighed a contented, “Ah, there we go—damn, I gotta say, I nailed that,” Turning to the back I added, “Groan if you agree, Petey!” In the back, he’d somehow ended up on the floor of the vehicle, having lost his balance at some point in all the confusion. I heard a groan. “Why thank you!~” Heh, he’s so cute.

The next few minutes passed in silence as I focused on shifting the car delicately enough to avoid swerving off the road; going at such a high speed makes it very easy to careen out of control. Learned that the hard way. The outskirts of Bullworth whipped past, and soon we turned onto the side road I wanted—plus, far fewer cars to weave around. Eventually, we came to a stand-still, and I breathed a sigh of relief; that was the portion that had some of the highest probability for the cops catching me or of somebody being seriously injured or dying.

I unbuckled myself and stepped out, opening the door behind the driver’s seat to reveal a cowering Femme Boy. I sighed as I grabbed a handful of his uniform. Now we entered the scared-shitless stage of the proceedings. He gave an undignified squawk as I dragged him out and said, “Come on Petey—we gotta get moving,” I sighed as he started squirming, trying to escape my grip. “You’ll have plenty of time to be scared out of your mind, don’t worry,” I had to press him against the side of the car to saw through the zip-tie binding his wrists. I have to make sure he doesn’t free Jimmy, but I didn’t have any reason to keep him locked up now. At the snap of plastic, Petey gazed at his hands as if he’d never seen them before quickly turning around and backing away from me.

I tried my best to smile reassuringly as I moved to the other side of the car. “Better?” He didn’t answer as I opened Jimbo’s door. I leaned against the door frame and maintained neutral eye contact. “Now, moron—I know you have trouble understanding English, so let me explain this very simply,” I leaned down to undo some of the duct-tape as I continued. “The first time around you kicked me in the face, so I don’t want a repeat this time,” Meeting his gaze steadily, I smirked a bit and quoted something from back in the first loop. “So; it’s up to you! You gonna play nice or what?” My smirk grew at the look of pure rage in his face, despite his grudging nod. I played along, saying, “Good boy,” Of course, as I was undoing his seatbelt I saw him prepare to give me a headbutt. I pulled my head out of the way at the last second, grabbing the back of his shirt as he missed to yank him out of the car. Just for the heck of it, I gave him a swift kick to the balls. His cry of pain was stifled by the gag, but I made sure to relish it anyhow.

As I moved around to the trunk, I laughed and sneered, “Ah, that’s what I love about you, Jimmy; you’ve always been so easy to control, even before I could predict your every action!” I popped the trunk, taking a few moments to browse through the gym bag full of packs of hundred-dollar bills that the police had confiscated from some poor criminal. I didn’t want to take the whole bag, since it was heavy and making Petey carry it was just adding humiliation to the conga line of trauma he’d be going through in the next few days. So, I picked the ones that had the fewest fives and ones stashed inside and stuffed them into my jacket. I wasn’t terribly worried, though; it could work.

As I shifted my attention to the wire-filled box and timer I had added, I heard Petey’s footsteps tentatively move over to where Jimmy’d collapsed on the ground. “Shit.... Jim–” but the moron started making anxious sounds. From what had happened last time around, I deduced he was frantically signaling Petey to try and do something to me. I leaned forward, pretending to be absorbed in what I was doing—really, this was just for show; I’d already set it to go off at the right time while waiting for him.

I could sense him trying to creep up on me from a mile away. Part of that can probably be attributed to my all-consuming obsession, but it’s also true that Petey isn’t exactly Batman. As he lunged for me I stepped back, grabbing his wrist as he passed and swinging him around so we were pressed close together—me against the bumper of the car, him against me. I shivered at the contact as I brought my mouth close to his ear and whispered, “Careful, now—it’s rude to interrupt somebody while they’re working on explosives.”

I knew it was stupid to do this; I already had the timer set, and maneuvering a massive camper out of this place is no small feat, so I was just giving myself less room for error as I let the seconds tick down. But as I wrapped my arms around him to pull us closer together I couldn’t care less. He let out a startled squeak that gave me the opportunity to reacquaint myself with the contours of the roof of his mouth and the shape of his teeth. The familiar warm tingling began to radiate out from where my mouth was latched onto his lips, and I let myself sink into his warmth, just a little; he was here! I wasn’t going to be crushed under a car, vaporized by a bomb, or dragged off to Happy Volts before I even got to see him. I snaked my arm around his neck to draw him even closer as the exhilarating buzzing just beneath my skin wiped the fear away—I wasn’t alone anymore.

A small, annoying portion of my brain piped up then, reminding me that we had to go. Of course—no rest for the wicked and all that. Reluctantly, I pulled away and took a shuddering breath, sighing as I tightened my arms around him. Burying my face in his hair, I muttered to myself, “God I missed you so fucking much....” Seven months with barely a fortnight’s worth of interaction with him gets lonely.

But it couldn’t last. Even with my eyes closed, I could hear the confusion in his voice as he stammered, “W-wh-whaa–!?..” I braced a hand on his shoulder and pushed him back a little, raising the other hand to place a finger on his lips.

“What’d I say about asking questions, Petey?” I turned around and hauled the containers of gasoline from the trunk as I continued. “Now, I’m going to need your help getting our massive friend into the RV, m’kay?” As I backed away to where the camper was located, I made sure to assess his mental state. He was staring at me with a dazed mixture of fear and confusion—right on track, then. I nodded in Jimmy’s direction, adding “So go pick whether you wanna carry the feet or the head,” He nodded automatically; that was good—if he has something to do, he doesn’t fight as much. I let out a breath as I turned around, feeling the lingering tingle on my skin when I set the cans down to fish out the keys. God, even after centuries he still lingers like no one else. Shaking my head, I consulted my mental list as I set the containers by the doorway. Hm.. the gas tank should be full, Petey and Jimmy already ate dinner at school, and the bomb was set to go off in fifteen minutes. I allowed myself a small smile as I made my way to the front of the vehicle and plopped down in front of the wheel; everything was on-schedule.

~~~

What’s interesting about constantly saying shocking things to people is that they don’t gasp or recoil right away. Usually they don’t even register what you’re saying as shocking—they just blink. Then, they snap into whatever reaction you were originally expecting, depending on the person. For Hopkins, it would probably be anger. Petey tends to go for a more ‘ stricken ’ look. Right now, though, he was giving Jimmy’s patented wat-whut-duh a run for its money. “You want to blow me? ” He leaned back, the customary disgust written all over his face. ~~~~~~Chapter 5: The Big Match~~~~~~

I was nervous. I see these guys almost every day nowadays, but usually that’s just in passing as I stuff earbuds in and ignore everybody else while I work out. Now, I was the center of attention as Preps surrounded the boxing ring and grumbled about ‘some scrawny, middle-class nobody’. I was just glad Jimmy was there to talk to me. He’d taken it upon himself to be my ‘coach’, and had even insisted on putting a towel on my shoulders before the match because it, apparently, ‘looked cool’. He was also doing the standard sports movie pre-match pep talk. “Don't fucking listen to these pussies, Pete! You got this, come on!” I looked over at Bif in the other corner uncertainly as he rolled his neck like this was no big deal.

I turned back toward Jimmy, who looked like he was excited as hell. I wished I could feel as excited as he looked. “I.. I don’t know, man, this.. um, I’m not so sure about this now…” I let out a heavy sigh. Being able to prove to myself that I could fight had sounded a lot more appealing when it only involved hypothetical violence.

He clapped me on the shoulder. “Come on, dude! You've been working for this for so long!” I gave him a side-long look; no matter how hard it worked, a fish couldn’t climb a tree. He just gave me a confident smirk. “Trust me, man. If you can hold your own against me, Bif don’t stand a fuckin’ chance,” I looked back at the other boy on the other side of the boxing ring; he was utterly relaxed, as if he wasn’t even worried. It was true, I had gotten to the point where I can hold my own against Jimmy… Right behind my head, he continued “Lookat ‘im—” He nudged me knowingly as he talked, like we were sharing in a secret. “He doesn’t even know what you’re fuckin’ capable of, dude!”

I looked at the floor, and I was ninety-percent sure I was blushing like crazy at the praise. “Come on, I’m not that good…” At that Jimmy grabbed my shoulders and turned me decisively around to face him, giving me a serious look.

“Pete, you are seriously going to kick this guy’s ass. Okay? I promise.”

I smiled at him. “Thanks so much, Jimmy.”

He just shrugged, leaning his forehead against mine. “Hey, what’re friends for?” That contact actually started to steady my nerves—it reminded me of that windy night in a trailer somewhere in New York. I could do this. This was what I’d been working for! I pulled away, giving Jimmy a more determined smile and nod. The bell then rang to begin the round, and Jimmy grinned at me, saying “Go get ‘em, tiger!” before stepping down from the ring. I smiled to myself—I really am lucky to have a friend like Jimmy.

Turning around, I walked up to meet Bif in the middle of the ring. The larger boy looked down (wayyy down) at me piteously. “Wow. You sure you wanna go up against the champ, kid?” and he tapped one gloved hand to my chest. “I mean, come on!” lightly pushing both gloves on my chest to emphasize his point, he added cockily “I won’t even need t o try with you, loser.”

I smirked—Jimmy was right, I really did feel ready. I shrugged, saying as respectfully as I could “Then I’m sure you have nothing to worry about,” To be fair, I couldn’t blame Bif for not finding me intimidating; I wouldn’t have been scared of a kid a whole head shorter than me, either.

I took a deep breath and locked my gaze on the Prep’s face, letting myself enter the numbing state of mind where I couldn’t hear anything, just my own breath. I spent the first minute or so dodging jabs, getting used to Bif’s fighting style. The larger boy focused on landing powerful hits and blocking—the only time I could get a hit in was when his attacks left him exposed somehow. As the round progressed, Bif became increasingly frustrated with his inability to hit me. Though he managed to land several hits, I recovered pretty well from each so he couldn’t chain hits like he clearly wanted to. He’d started to resort to taunting, but it really wasn’t very effective. Most of it was about my lack of wealth, which just made me roll my eyes; wow, a Prep teasing somebody about money. How original.

Jimmy shook my shoulder as the round ended and I made my way to the corner, very out of breath, but satisfied. Dodging all those power hits takes a lot out of me, but it’s kinda fun. “You’re doing great! Just two more rounds to go and you’ll have proof you can deal with any psychos that show up, right?” Jimmy waved a water bottle in my face, sporting a grin. I smiled briefly as I took the bottle—I was more worried about sucking the water down. Jimmy kept talking—he was practically hopping up and down he was so excited. “Okay, so you got really good right at the end there. Whatever you did, keep doing it and that bullshit title is as good as yours, man!”

Clapping me on the shoulder one last time, he hopped down just as the bell to begin the next round rung.

Bif didn’t bother with any subtly, opening with a right hook. I dodged only to realize it was a feint, since the left half of my face erupted into pain. Shit—I had to get out of range. I hopped back, letting the force of the blow move me away. Bif was clearly very frustrated— I’m a far cry from a heavy hitter, but I had become very good at expending a minimal amount of energy to dodge opponents. I'd trained with Jimmy, after all, and he’s really light on his feet for somebody who’s so strong. I shook my head—mind on the MATCH!—only to need to roll out of range of another powerful hit. I heard the larger boy growl at his opponent slipping from his grasp yet again. "What's the matter, pauper, are you afraid I might put you on welfare!?"

I knew I needed to get some damage in, so I switched from defense to offence. Unfortunately, that left me open and I ended up face-down on the mat by the middle of the round. As I gritted my teeth and dragged myself up, Jimmy yelled at me “C’mon, Pete! Pretend he’s Gary or some shit!” I flinched at the name as I finished getting up before turning back to Bif but did my best to ignore it. Come on! I could do this!

Unfortunately, it seemed Bif had heard Jimmy. “Gary? Who’s Gary, loser?” I had mostly been keeping a neutral expression up until this point since I was concentrating. But when he mentioned Gary, my face automatically twisted into a scowl.

“Shut up, man,” Bif grinned as I looked for an opening—unfortunately, it seemed they don’t give out that champion title to just anybody; he really is a good boxer.

“Ah, it speaks! I didn’t know poor people could talk!” He laughed as I flicked my eyes to the clock. There were only fifteen seconds left! “Ah, that Gary Smith boy, right?” I stiffened. “Ha, he your boyfriend or something? That why he hasn’t been around?”

I spat “Shut up!” before I could stop myself. I could feel the rage simmering just beneath the surface—I was already warm from the physical exercise, but it felt like my skin was suddenly too hot. As the bell rang, I knew I’d made a mistake from Bif’s cocky grin at knowing my ‘weakness’.

Retreating to my own corner, I tried to get myself back under control. “Hey, you all right?” I shot Jimmy a pleading look, shaking my head. I flashed suddenly on Gary running his tongue over my dick and flinched. God, not now! “No, man, that’s good! Imagine Bif is Gary, okay? You just gotta channel it right.”

I shook my head, voice desperate. “But he’s not Gary!”

Jimmy looked like he was about to say something, but the third bell rung at that point; he threw me a thumbs-up and added quickly “You can do it!” as he hopped down. Welp. I turned back to the center of the ring, trying to ignore the flood of images that had decided to overtake my brain.

It must’ve shown on my face somehow, because Bif then said “Aw, missing your boyfriend?” right before the second bell to actually begin the round.

I couldn’t move—I was too busy staring at him with pure loathing. I managed to grind out “You don’t know shit.”

I forced myself to move already, dodging another jab even as a memory of Gary looking at me with a frighteningly unquenchable thirst lodged itself in the forefront of my mind. I only narrowly managed to avoid the hit, which seemed to raise Bif’s spirits. Clearly he thought he had the key to victory. “Ah, I’ll bet you wanted his money. Started playing gold digger?” He shrugged as I felt my entire body start to vibrate. Only the barest sliver of reason was keeping me from trying to tear this asshole apart.

I yelled “SHUT. UP!” and punctuated the words with two jabs that finally met their mark. Who does this douche think he is, talking like he knows me? Like he knows Gary!?

Bif grunted, recovering from my surprise hits, but he swung at me and connected again. Honestly though, I was beyond caring at this point; I just took the punch so I could swipe again. I swore to myself when Bif evaded them. He continued conversationally “Well it’s too bad that he’s gone, a loser like you could really use somebody like him—” He shrugged, adding something more that I couldn’t hear.

I shook my head; Gary calling me ‘Femme Boy’ so many times that it had actually started to sound like a compliment reverberated through my head. I glared daggers at Bif and muttered “You don’t fucking know him” as I took various swings at him, each more vicious than the last. But my punching had become nothing more than unorganized flailing that Bif was easily able to block or dodge. Crap! I stepped away, forcing myself to take a deep breath. I reminded myself of all the training I’d gone through with Jimmy, and squeezed the rage that was pulsing through my veins into the framework of boxing—read your opponent, wait until they’re open, and hit as hard as you can. I re-joined the fight, using this newfound laser-focus to dodge multiple jabs. I finally found an opening, and started just fucking wailing on him, letting the memory of feeling utterly powerless as I watched my only friend waste away before my eyes wash through me. I sure as hell wasn’t powerless now. As he staggered back, I squeezed my eyes shut as some of the more graphic memories resurfaced, making me retch a little. I forced my eyes back open, saw he was about to take a swing—but he’d left himself open, and a mental image of Gary’s face smeared with blood and gleeful anticipation as he was about to attack Jimmy sent my blood boiling. I couldn’t care less about being hit myself by this point; all I could see was red, and I wanted somebody hurt. At some point, though, I registered that Bif wasn’t fighting back—he’d fallen down, and wasn’t getting back up.

I blinked, backing away as the bile rose in my throat—my adrenaline rush slowly died down, allowing the sound of outraged Preppies and an enthusiastically hollering Jimmy to reach my ears. Even so, they sounded muffled and far away. The rage had come on so fast I was still reeling—my skin was crawling again, and I was having trouble breathing. I scrabbled to get the boxing gloves off, throwing them away as far as I could, and pressing both palms into my eyes. I wasn’t sure what was stronger, the need to sob until I couldn’t breathe or the need to throw up whatever I’d eaten that morning. Either way, my throat was so closed up that I couldn’t do anything but tremble as the crash set in.

Gary. Gary, Gary, GARY! It feels like he’s all I ever think about! My knees gave way and I collapsed gracelessly onto the mat, my body apparently deciding that crying would be more appropriate for the moment. For fuck’s sake, why do I have to feel this way? A memory of Gary stroking me immediately made my throat fill with bile and forced out a sob. I hadn’t liked any of that! Then why was I so angry when Bif had said that shit about Gary? Why do I care about him even with everything he’s fucking done!?

I shifted to sitting on my butt, and wrapped my hands around my knees as I took some deep breaths to quiet the sobs a little. Why did I need to feel this shitty? I considered some more memories—one of that first night, when Gary had stabbed the table to avoid discussing his motivations; another of Gary promising he was just going to make me feel really, really good as he rubbed my penis; Gary staring at me for hours while I doodled, his expression resigned; Gary kissing me in the dark and whispering ‘thank you’ in my ear over and over again after a handjob; I shuddered. In disgust, partly, but all those memories made me feel more than just gross—they felt so… intimate, like I’d taken something without him even realizing it.

As I took more shuddering breaths to calm myself, I felt somebody rubbing circles on my back. Jimmy. He wasn’t saying anything, but I felt better just knowing he was there. I got your back. I uncurled myself, wiping my eyes and nose with the back of my hand. Turning to Jimmy, I had to explain. “I—” my throat closed up, but I just waited for it to open back up. “I hate feeling this way…”

Jimmy nodded, still rubbing my back as he looked at me with empathy. “I know, man. Ya just gotta work through it,” I was suddenly aware of a great deal of muttering behind me, which caused Jimmy to glare over his shoulder. “Hey, why don’t ya’ll piss off, huh? Give your new champ some respect!”

I snickered softly as the Preps responded with customary prickly hostility. Raising both hands to cover my eyes, I realized something; I don’t have to be angry with him. Moving so my hands were supporting my own weight as Jimmy got up and started a shouting match with the others in the room, I realized I wanted to forgive Gary. I frowned, memories of the sex stuff returning. But… I recalled the anger from earlier, my grip on the mat tightening. Forgiving him would be so much easier than staying angry with him…

But an authoritative voice broke me out of my contemplation. “You disgust me!” I looked up to see Derby looking at Bif like he was some dog shit stuck to the bottom of his shoe.

But before he could get another word in, Jimmy cut in with “Yeah, right back at’chya, fuckface!” I saw Derby’s eyes widen in shock before he started glaring at Jimmy. I couldn’t see his face from this angle, but Jimmy’s stance was very relaxed. He had beaten these guys four times by now, after all—he had plenty of reason to be cocky.

Darby sneered his next comment directly at Jimmy. “It takes more than victory to become a champion, gutter-snipe,” Turning around, he addressed his fellows with what probably counted for a rousing speech as I started pushing myself back to my feet. “It takes breeding, and nepotism, and snobbery—” Turning back to Jimmy, he spat “Things I’m sure some food-stamp bastard like you could never understand,” I grimaced, looking at Jimmy carefully. Stuff about his family was a huge sore spot for him. I put a hand on his shoulder questioningly as he cracked his knuckles. He nodded a little in my direction at the contact, a silent thanks for the support as Derby continued getting the Preps riled up. I was just relieved Jimmy was okay. “Gentlemen, are we going to let some middle-class nobody come in and beat up our friend, Bif?” I flinched, looking down at Bif. Yeesh… I really did beat him up… He was coughing as he pushed himself up to his hands and knees, and I felt the sour sensation of guilt in my gut. Sheesh, I didn’t even know I could hurt people like that.

I shook my head as I walked up to the boxer, ignoring the chorus of “NO!” in the background from the small number of Preps. It wasn’t fair for me to win because of such a fluke; he couldn’t have known that Gary was such a sore spot for me. Looking at the pain I’d caused, I didn’t really care about winning anymore, anyway.

“Then what are we going to do!?” As Derby kept talking, I crouched down next to Bif, who glared at me. But before he said anything, I extended a hand to him, trying to give him a warm smile. Plus, I really should have been more mature in responding to the taunting.

The loud cries of “Beat him back to the subdivision!” kind of undermined my attempt at being non-threatening, but oh well.

Jimmy cut through the cacophony of ‘YEAH!’s as he vaulted over the edge of the ring, shouting “Hey, you wanna get to him, you gotta go through me first, blue-bitches!” That got Bif’s attention, and he began trying to push himself back to his feet.

I put a hand on his shoulder to keep him from moving too much. “Whoa, hey, it’s okay—are you alright?” I scanned the other kid’s face for any signs of a serious injury, worrying my lip; I couldn’t recall feeling any crunches or snaps, but the seconds-long round was a blur in my memory—it had felt like minutes to me, so I didn’t trust myself to remember.

Bif glanced back at me, the confusion returning for a moment before shifting to anger. He sneered “What do you want, loser?” It sounded like he wanted to continue, but he was interrupted by some coughing.

Rolling my eyes at the irony of using the term ‘loser’ in this case, I replied “I don’t—I mean, I was just checking to make sure you’re not hurt.” Seemed like he was okay—he was moving his limbs and face alright. I rubbed an arm awkwardly and moved to sit next to him, adding “I’m… I’m sorry I went off on you, I shouldn’t have lost my head like that,” I stared blankly at the mat, recalling the surge of anger at what the boxer had said about Gary—it was like he was assuming he knew Gary, when he so obviously doesn’t know him. I frowned. But… why does that bother me so much?

A loud laugh from my left broke me out of my thoughts and drew my attention back to Bif. The other teenager gave me a superior look as he sneered “Are you seriously apologizing for fighting me?” He’d finally stopped coughing enough to be able to shift off his knees and sit down.

I laughed a little, shrugging. “Yeah, I suppose I am!” I sighed, adding “I should’ve been more mature and ignored what you were saying.” I smiled more genuinely as a bit of relief sprung up in my chest. I don’t know Bif very well, so it wasn’t like I was crying tears of joy or anything, but it made me feel a little better after the dark place my thoughts had gone during the fight. “Hey, want some water?” I got up before he answered. I wanted something to drink anyway, I pretty thirsty.

Bif sounded confused when he replied automatically “Um, sure?” Luckily, he didn’t sound hostile anymore. As I walked over to the corner of the ring where Jimmy had set my water, the sounds of fighting drifted down from the bar upstairs. I sighed. It’s like they didn’t even see me apologize to Bif. I swear, the people in this town are freakin’ crazy. Picking up the water, I gulped some down as I moved back to where the other boy was before holding it out questioningly as I sat down. “…thanks?” Bif accepted the water, moving to lift the bottle directly to his mouth before stopping and looking from the bottle to me and back. Instead he poured the water into his mouth without touching it to his lips. I had to suppress an eye-roll; seriously? Do poor people have cooties now or something? When he was done, he looked all around the room as he fiddled with the bottle before meeting my eyes, saying “I guess I’m… uh, sorry for saying that stuff.”

I started—that had been the last thing I’d expected—before waving a hand dismissively. “It’s okay, man.” I sighed, adding “You couldn’t have known how… um, sensitive a topic that is for me.”

After that we sat in relative silence for a while, just listening to the sounds of continued fighting. I could hear the ‘twang’ of a slingshot coupled with some muffled cackling and taunts. It sounded like Jimmy was just dragging it out. I don’t think I’ll ever get why he likes fighting and violence so much. “Yeah, I can’t believe Smith is into guys!” I started a bit, snapping my gaze to Bif, who looked a bit pensive before shrugging, looking at me a bit awkwardly. “Who knew, ehh?”

I closed my eyes, choosing my words carefully. “Look; if you know anything about me, know that I’m not in any kind of relationship with Gary,” But even as I said it, I flashed on other memories. Meeting Gary at the ‘beginning’ of the year where he’d given me the stupid nick-name; the way his face had lit up when I thanked him for buying me a sketchbook and high-end drawing supplies; that one time he’d shown up at my house for Halloween completely uninvited one year and dragged me out trick-or-treating despite my fear of actually seeing and interacting with other kids from town; how relaxed he’d been explaining freaking black holes to me. He definitely isn’t just some around-town acquaintance like he had been before—but he’s certainly not a friend either… Hell, I hadn’t even seen Gary for a couple of years. The only inkling Jimmy and I had that he wasn’t dead was that the team hired to search for him was constantly seeing him in security footage in various locales, but they never seemed to be able to actually find him.

Bif laughed derisively, saying “I know, right? That guy is a real weirdo,” I snorted at that; man was that ever true! “Haha, yeah. This one time, my parents made me go over to his house or something and he legit wouldn’t even talk to me; just said something about ‘refusing to lower his IQ’,” I laughed despite myself—that was Gary, all right! Bif looked pretty relaxed, shrugging as he added “My father says the Smiths are having a public-relations nightmare trying to find him,” He scratched his arm absently, adding “Wonder what happened to him, anyway?” I shrugged; I’d considered the question myself, but I honestly haven’t the foggiest. He’d left so abruptly that Jimmy and I had just shrugged our shoulders and been happy he was gone—but that had been, like, three or four yea–er, loops ago. It was getting a little weird.

Our impromptu gab sesh was interrupted when the door to the bar upstairs slammed open, and Jimmy shouted “‘Ey yo Pete! Ya still around?” He spotting me waving from the railing, and added “Cool” as he walked over to the staircase. He grinned, saying slyly “So ya wanna go vandalize a Prep’s house or somethin’ to celebrate?” I saw Bif scowl at that, clearly ready to shout an insult at him, but I held a hand out in a ‘hold on’ gesture as I pushed myself to a standing position.

He was heavy “—you don’t seriously think that was a fair win, do you Jimmy?” I turned to give my friend a patronizing look as he descended the stairs, at which point he finally spotted who I was with.

When he did, he snorted. “Hey, douchey-bags,” Looking between the two of us for a moment, he rolled his eyes as I walked over toward him, ducking to go under the ropes and sliding off the edge of the ring-slash-platform. “Lemmie guess, you’re friends with this guy now.”

Jimmy was about to reply but Bif beat him to it. “Hey what happened? Where’re my friends?” I cringed a little in sympathy.

Jimmy snorted. “Upstairs, licking their wounds, I bet; beat the shit outta ‘em,” He threw Bif a threatening glare, adding “Nobody fucks with my friends—got it, trust-fund baby?”

Jimmy sighed, stepping back. Bif started, then began glaring at me. “What’dya mean who’s got it? You tryin’ to make fun of me, loser?”

Sheesh… are all rich people as quick to jump to conclusions as Gary? I held my hands up in a placating manner. “No, not at all! I’m trying to say that I don’t think that was a fair fight, so you should stay the champion,” I sighed, looking sidelong in Jimmy’s direction pointedly. “Of course, we could have discussed this with the people who run the gym and, by extension, the tournament, if they weren’t unconscious on the floor upstairs.”

But Jimmy either didn’t hear my annoyance or didn’t care. He shifted so he was looking me more directly in the eye, his mouth hanging open. “Pete, are you serious? You’ve been working to do this for a year and a half, and now you’re just gonna throw it away!?”

Having lived through a few loops myself I probably had a better grasp of the concept than most, but the sheer scale of what Gary must’ve gone through was… well, horrifying.

I sighed; Jimmy never bends when it comes to Gary. It’s like if he thinks of Gary as anything other than some one-dimensional evil villain it would be like kicking the shit out of his mother or something.

<> 

Eventually, Bif and I parted ways, and I went out to find Jimmy. He was, not surprisingly, unhappy with this development. “What are you, some fuckin’ Xiaolin temple monk or something? All ‘one with all’ and shit?” Were his exact words. But I didn’t care—Jimmy could protest all he wanted, but I’d made up my mind; I care more about my own sanity than holding a grudge.

<new chapter 6: Gary Alone?>

~~~~~~~~~~~~

Highway underpasses. River banks. Bus stops. Homeless shelters. Locations and faces melted and blurred together into a formless mass as time passed. I had to force myself to eat, to avoid danger, to keep myself out of harm’s way. Pe… he had said not to kill myself, but there was no way to know whether that extended to putting myself into situations knowing it was likely that I would die. It was difficult. Incredibly so.
